Exposing LLM Safety Gaps Through Mathematical Encoding:New Attacks and Systematic Analysis
Authors: Haoyu Zhang, Mohammad Zandsalimy, Shanu Sushmita
First: 2026-05-05T07:25:33+00:00 · Latest: 2026-05-05T07:25:33+00:00
Comments: 16 pages, 2 figures, 4 tables. Accepted as a long paper at the 39th Canadian Conference on Artificial Intelligence (Canadian AI 2026)
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Large language models (LLMs) employ safety mechanisms to prevent harmful outputs, yet these defenses primarily rely on semantic pattern matching. We show that encoding harmful prompts as coherent mathematical problems -- using formalisms such as set theory, formal logic, and quantum mechanics -- bypasses these filters at high rates, achieving 46%--56% average attack success across eight target models and two established benchmarks. Crucially, the effectiveness depends not on mathematical notation itself, but on whether a helper LLM deeply reformulates the harmful content into a genuine mathematical problem: rule-based encodings that apply mathematical formatting without such reformulation perform no better than unencoded baselines. We introduce a novel Formal Logic encoding that achieves attack success comparable to Set Theory, demonstrating that this vulnerability generalizes across mathematical formalisms. Additional experiments with repeat post-processing confirm that these attacks are robust to simple prompt augmentation. Notably, newer models (GPT-5, GPT-5-Mini) show substantially greater robustness than older models, though they remain vulnerable. Our findings highlight fundamental gaps in current safety frameworks and motivate defenses that reason about mathematical structure rather than surface-level semantics.
中文标题/摘要
标题：通过数学编码揭示大型语言模型的安全漏洞：新攻击与系统分析
大型语言模型（LLMs）采用安全机制以防止有害输出，但这些防御主要依赖于语义模式匹配。我们展示了将有害提示编码为连贯的数学问题——使用集合论、形式逻辑和量子力学等形式——可以高效绕过这些过滤器，在八个目标模型和两个已建立基准上实现46%至56%的平均攻击成功率。关键在于，效果并不依赖于数学符号本身，而在于辅助LLM是否将有害内容深度重构为真正的数学问题：仅应用数学格式的基于规则的编码表现与未编码基线无异。我们引入了一种新颖的形式逻辑编码，其攻击成功率与集合论相当，表明这种脆弱性在数学形式中具有普遍性。对重复后处理的额外实验确认这些攻击对简单提示增强具有鲁棒性。值得注意的是，较新的模型（GPT-5，GPT-5-Mini）显示出比旧模型更大的鲁棒性，尽管它们仍然脆弱。我们的发现突显了当前安全框架中的基本缺口，并激励针对数学结构而非表面语义进行推理的防御措施。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the limitations of current safety mechanisms in large language models (LLMs), which primarily rely on semantic pattern matching to prevent harmful outputs. Previous methods have struggled with encoding harmful prompts effectively, leading to vulnerabilities that the proposed approach seeks to exploit by reformulating harmful content into coherent mathematical problems using formal logics such as set theory. This novel method demonstrates that the success of attacks is not merely due to mathematical notation but hinges on deep reformulation by a helper LLM, achieving an average attack success rate of 46%–56% across eight models and two benchmarks. The paper contributes to the understanding of safety gaps in LLMs and introduces a new Formal Logic encoding that matches the effectiveness of Set Theory, revealing that these vulnerabilities are consistent across different mathematical frameworks. The findings indicate that while newer models show improved robustness, they still exhibit vulnerabilities, underscoring the need for safety mechanisms that consider mathematical structure rather than just semantic patterns.
本研究关注大型语言模型（LLM）现有安全机制的局限性，这些机制主要依赖语义模式匹配来防止有害输出。以往的方法在绕过这些防御时面临困难，而所提出的方法则引入将有害提示编码为连贯的数学问题，利用集合论和形式逻辑等形式主义。这种方法有效地绕过了现有的过滤器，在八个目标模型和两个基准测试中实现了46%到56%的平均攻击成功率，突显了当前安全框架中的重大漏洞。研究方法包括一种新颖的形式逻辑编码，其攻击成功率与集合论相当，表明这种脆弱性在不同数学形式主义中具有普遍性。研究结果表明，尽管较新的模型表现出更强的鲁棒性，但它们仍然容易受到攻击，强调了需要关注数学结构而不仅仅是表面语义的防御措施。
From Prompt to Physical Actuation: Holistic Threat Modeling of LLM-Enabled Robotic Systems
Authors: Neha Nagaraja, Hayretdin Bahsi, Carlo R. da Cunha
First: 2026-04-29T23:44:07+00:00 · Latest: 2026-05-04T05:54:12+00:00
Comments: Submitted to 23rd Annual International Conference on Privacy, Security, and Trust (PST2026)
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
As large language models are integrated into autonomous robotic systems for task planning and control, compromised inputs or unsafe model outputs can propagate through the planning pipeline to physical-world consequences. Although prior work has studied robotic cybersecurity, adversarial perception attacks, and LLM safety independently, no existing study traces how these threat categories interact and propagate across trust boundaries in a unified architectural model. We address this gap by modeling an LLM-enabled autonomous robot in an edge-cloud architecture as a hierarchical Data Flow Diagram and applying STRIDE-per-interaction analysis across six boundary-crossing interaction points using a three-category taxonomy of Conventional Cyber Threats, Adversarial Threats, and Conversational Threats. The analysis reveals that these categories converge at the same boundary crossings, and we trace three cross-boundary attack chains from external entry points to unsafe physical actuation, each exposing a distinct architectural property: the absence of independent semantic validation between user input and actuator dispatch, cross-modal translation from visual perception to language-model instruction, and unmediated boundary crossing through provider-side tool use. To our knowledge, this is the first DFD-based threat analysis integrating all three threat categories across the full perception-planning-actuation pipeline of an LLM-enabled robotic system.
中文标题/摘要
标题：从提示到物理执行：LLM驱动机器人系统的整体威胁建模
随着大型语言模型被集成到自主机器人系统中进行任务规划和控制，受损的输入或不安全的模型输出可能会通过规划流程传播到物理世界的后果。尽管之前的研究独立地研究了机器人网络安全、对抗感知攻击和LLM安全，但没有现有研究追踪这些威胁类别如何在统一的架构模型中相互作用和传播。我们通过将LLM驱动的自主机器人建模为边缘-云架构中的分层数据流图，并在六个跨边界交互点应用基于交互的STRIDE分析，使用常规网络威胁、对抗威胁和对话威胁的三类分类法来填补这一空白。分析表明，这些类别在相同的边界交叉处汇聚，我们追踪了三条跨边界攻击链，从外部入口点到不安全的物理执行，每条链暴露出一个独特的架构特性：用户输入与执行器调度之间缺乏独立的语义验证、从视觉感知到语言模型指令的跨模态翻译，以及通过提供方工具使用的无中介边界跨越。据我们所知，这是首个基于DFD的威胁分析，整合了所有三类威胁，覆盖了LLM驱动机器人系统的完整感知-规划-执行流程。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the integration of large language models (LLMs) into autonomous robotic systems, highlighting the risks of compromised inputs and unsafe outputs that can lead to physical-world consequences. Previous studies have examined aspects of robotic cybersecurity and adversarial attacks separately, failing to provide a comprehensive view of how these threats interact across trust boundaries. This paper proposes a holistic threat modeling approach using a hierarchical Data Flow Diagram (DFD) and STRIDE-per-interaction analysis to evaluate six interaction points within an edge-cloud architecture. The findings reveal converging threat categories at boundary crossings and identify three distinct attack chains that lead to unsafe actuation, emphasizing critical architectural vulnerabilities. This work contributes a unified framework for analyzing threats in LLM-enabled robotic systems, marking the first comprehensive threat analysis across the perception-planning-actuation pipeline.

Useless but Safe? Benchmarking Utility Recovery with User Intent Clarification in Multi-Turn Conversations
Authors: Mingqian Zheng, Malia Morgan, Liwei Jiang, Carolyn Rose, Maarten Sap
First: 2026-04-29T18:37:18+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-29T18:37:18+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Current LLM safety alignment techniques improve model robustness against adversarial attacks, but overlook whether and how LLMs can recover helpfulness when benign users clarify their intent. We introduce CarryOnBench, the first interactive benchmark that measures whether LLMs can revise their interpretation of user intent and recover utility, while remaining safe through multi-turn conversations. Starting from 398 seemingly harmful queries with benign underlying intents, we simulate 5,970 conversations by varying user follow-up sequences, evaluating 14 models on both intent-aligned utility and safety. CarryOnBench yields 1,866 different conversation flows of 4--12 turns, totaling 23,880 model responses. We design Ben-Util, a checklist-based metric that evaluates how well each model response fulfills the user's benign information need using atomic items. At turn one, models fulfill only 10.5--37.6% of the user's benign information need. When the same query includes the benign intent upfront, models fulfill 25.1--72.1%, confirming that models withhold information due to intent misinterpretation, not limited knowledge. With benign clarifications in multi-turn conversations, 13 of 14 models approach or exceed this single-turn baseline, yet recovery cost varies across models. We identify three failure modes invisible to single-turn evaluations: utility lock-in, where a model rarely updates despite clarification; unsafe recovery, where a model updates at disproportionate safety cost; and repetitive recovery, where a model recycles prior responses rather than providing new information. Moreover, conversations converge to similar harmfulness levels regardless of how conservative the model starts. These findings expose a gap that single-turn evaluations miss -- whether a model is appropriately cautious or simply unresponsive to clarified user intent.
中文标题/摘要
标题：无用但安全？在多轮对话中通过用户意图澄清基准测试实用性恢复
当前的LLM安全对齐技术提高了模型对抗攻击的鲁棒性，但忽视了LLM在良性用户澄清意图时是否以及如何恢复有用性。我们引入CarryOnBench，这是第一个交互式基准，测量LLM在多轮对话中是否能够修正对用户意图的解释并恢复实用性，同时保持安全。从398个看似有害的查询开始，这些查询具有良性的潜在意图，我们通过变化用户后续序列模拟了5,970个对话，评估了14个模型在意图对齐的实用性和安全性方面的表现。CarryOnBench产生了1,866种不同的对话流程，轮次为4到12，总计23,880个模型响应。我们设计了Ben-Util，这是一个基于清单的指标，评估每个模型响应在多大程度上满足用户的良性信息需求。在第一轮中，模型仅满足用户良性信息需求的10.5%到37.6%。当同一查询在前面包含良性意图时，模型满足25.1%到72.1%，确认模型因意图误解而抑制信息，而不是知识有限。在多轮对话中，经过良性澄清，14个模型中有13个接近或超过这一单轮基线，但恢复成本在模型之间有所不同。我们识别出三种在单轮评估中不可见的失败模式：实用性锁定，即模型在澄清后很少更新；不安全恢复，即模型以不成比例的安全成本进行更新；以及重复恢复，即模型回收先前的响应而不是提供新信息。此外，无论模型起始多么保守，对话都趋向于相似的有害性水平。这些发现揭示了单轮评估所忽视的一个差距——模型是否适当地谨慎，或仅仅对澄清的用户意图无反应。
Summary / 总结
This research addresses the limitations of current large language model (LLM) safety alignment techniques, which enhance robustness against adversarial attacks but fail to assess how LLMs can recover helpfulness when users clarify their intent in multi-turn conversations. Previous methods primarily focused on single-turn evaluations, neglecting the dynamics of conversation and the potential for models to misinterpret benign user intents, leading to inadequate responses. The proposed approach, CarryOnBench, is an interactive benchmark that simulates 5,970 conversations to evaluate 14 models on their ability to revise intent interpretations while maintaining safety. The study reveals that at the first turn, models fulfill only 10.5–37.6% of benign information needs, but with clarifications, 13 out of 14 models improve their performance, highlighting issues such as utility lock-in and unsafe recovery. Policy-Grounded Safety Evaluation of 20 Large Language Models
Authors: Juan Manuel Contreras
First: 2025-07-19T18:49:16+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-29T15:54:46+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
As large language models (LLMs) become increasingly integrated into real-world applications, scalable and rigorous safety evaluation is essential. This paper introduces Aymara AI, a programmatic platform for generating and administering customized, policy-grounded safety evaluations. Aymara AI transforms natural-language safety policies into adversarial prompts and scores model responses using an AI-based rater validated against human judgments. We demonstrate its capabilities through the Aymara LLM Risk and Responsibility Matrix, which evaluates 20 commercially available LLMs across 10 real-world safety domains. Results reveal wide performance disparities, with mean safety scores ranging from 86.2% to 52.4%. While models performed well in well-established safety domains such as Misinformation (mean = 95.7%), they consistently failed in more complex or underspecified domains, notably Privacy & Impersonation (mean = 24.3%). Analyses of Variance confirmed that safety scores differed significantly across both models and domains (p < .05). These findings underscore the inconsistent and context-dependent nature of LLM safety and highlight the need for scalable, customizable tools like Aymara AI to support responsible AI development and oversight.
中文标题/摘要
标题：基于政策的20个大型语言模型的安全评估
随着大型语言模型（LLMs）越来越多地融入现实应用，规模化和严格的安全评估变得至关重要。本文介绍了Aymara AI，一个用于生成和管理定制化、基于政策的安全评估的程序平台。Aymara AI将自然语言安全政策转化为对抗性提示，并使用经过人类判断验证的AI评分者对模型响应进行评分。我们通过Aymara LLM风险与责任矩阵展示其能力，该矩阵评估了20个商业可用的LLMs在10个现实安全领域的表现。结果显示，性能差异显著，平均安全评分范围从86.2%到52.4%。虽然模型在虚假信息等成熟安全领域表现良好（平均=95.7%），但在更复杂或不明确的领域（特别是隐私与冒充）中表现不佳（平均=24.3%）。方差分析确认，安全评分在模型和领域之间存在显著差异（p < .05）。这些发现强调了LLM安全性的不一致性和依赖于上下文的特性，并突显了像Aymara AI这样的可扩展、可定制工具在支持负责任的AI开发和监督中的必要性。

Evaluating LLM Safety Under Repeated Inference via Accelerated Prompt Stress Testing
Authors: Keita Broadwater
First: 2026-02-12T10:09:13+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-28T16:38:37+00:00
Comments: 23 pages, 9 figures; editorial and LaTeX revisions for clarity; improved presentation of methodology and results; updated figures, tables, and float placement; clarified temperature sensitivity and deployment-risk analysis; expanded reporting from the same experiments; results unchanged in substance
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Traditional benchmarks for large language models (LLMs), such as HELM and AIR-BENCH, primarily assess safety through breadth-oriented evaluation across diverse tasks and risk categories. However, real-world deployment often exposes a different class of risk: operational failures that arise under repeated inference on identical or near-identical prompts rather than from broad task-level underperformance. In high-stakes settings, response consistency and safety under sustained use are therefore critical. We introduce Accelerated Prompt Stress Testing (APST), a depth-oriented evaluation framework inspired by highly accelerated stress testing in reliability engineering. APST repeatedly samples identical prompts under controlled operational conditions (such as decoding temperature) to surface latent failure modes including hallucinations, refusal inconsistency, and unsafe completions. Rather than treating failures as isolated events, APST models them as stochastic outcomes of repeated inference and uses Bernoulli and binomial formulations to estimate per-inference failure probabilities. Applying APST to multiple instruction-tuned LLMs evaluated on AIR-BENCH 2024--derived safety and security prompts, we find that models with comparable shallow-evaluation scores can exhibit substantially different empirical failure rates under repeated sampling. These results show that single-sample or low-depth evaluation can obscure meaningful differences in deployment-relevant reliability. APST complements existing benchmark methodologies by providing a practical framework for estimating failure frequency under sustained use and comparing safety reliability across models and decoding configurations.
中文标题/摘要
标题：通过加速提示压力测试评估大语言模型的安全性
传统的大语言模型（LLMs）基准，如HELM和AIR-BENCH，主要通过在多样任务和风险类别中的广度评估来评估安全性。然而，实际部署往往暴露出另一类风险：在相同或近似相同的提示下重复推理所导致的操作失败，而不是广泛任务级别的表现不佳。在高风险环境中，响应一致性和持续使用下的安全性至关重要。我们引入了加速提示压力测试（APST），这是一个受可靠性工程中高度加速压力测试启发的深度评估框架。APST在受控操作条件下（如解码温度）重复采样相同的提示，以揭示潜在的失败模式，包括幻觉、拒绝不一致和不安全的完成。APST将失败视为重复推理的随机结果，并使用伯努利和二项式公式来估计每次推理的失败概率。将APST应用于多个在AIR-BENCH 2024上评估的指令调优LLMs的安全和安全提示，我们发现具有可比浅层评估分数的模型在重复采样下可能表现出显著不同的经验失败率。这些结果表明，单样本或低深度评估可能掩盖在部署相关可靠性方面的有意义差异。APST通过提供一个实用框架来估计持续使用下的失败频率，并比较模型和解码配置之间的安全可靠性，补充了现有的基准方法。
Summary / 总结
This article addresses the limitations of traditional benchmarks for evaluating large language models (LLMs), which often focus on broad task performance rather than the operational risks associated with repeated inference on similar prompts. Previous methods fail to capture the nuances of response consistency and safety in real-world applications, particularly in high-stakes environments. The proposed Accelerated Prompt Stress Testing (APST) framework offers a depth-oriented evaluation approach that systematically samples identical prompts under controlled conditions to identify latent failure modes such as hallucinations and inconsistent responses. By modeling failures as stochastic outcomes and employing Bernoulli and binomial formulations, APST reveals significant differences in empirical failure rates among models that appear similar in shallow evaluations. This methodology enhances existing benchmarks by providing a practical means to estimate failure frequency during sustained use, thereby improving the assessment of safety reliability across various models and configurations.

Adaptive Prompt Embedding Optimization for LLM Jailbreaking
Authors: Miles Q. Li, Benjamin C. M. Fung, Boyang Li, Radin Hamidi Rad, Ebrahim Bagheri
First: 2026-04-27T20:39:08+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-27T20:39:08+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Existing white-box jailbreak attacks against aligned LLMs typically append discrete adversarial suffixes to the user prompt, which visibly alters the prompt and operates in a combinatorial token space. Prior work has avoided directly optimizing the embeddings of the original prompt tokens, presumably because perturbing them risks destroying the prompt's semantic content. We propose Prompt Embedding Optimization (PEO), a multi-round white-box jailbreak that directly optimizes the embeddings of the original prompt tokens without appending any adversarial tokens, and show that the concern is unfounded: the optimized embeddings remain close enough to their originals that the visible prompt string is preserved exactly after nearest-token projection, and quantitative analysis shows the model's responses stay on topic for the large majority of prompts. PEO combines continuous embedding-space optimization with structured continuation targets and an adaptive failure-focused schedule. Counterintuitively, later PEO rounds can benefit from heuristic composite response scaffolds that are not natural standalone templates, yet ASR-Judge shows that the resulting gains are not merely empty formatting or scaffold-only outputs. Across two standard harmful-behavior benchmarks and competing white-box attacks spanning discrete suffix search, appended adversarial embeddings, and search-based adversarial generation, PEO outperforms all of them in our experiments.
中文标题/摘要
标题：用于大型语言模型越狱的自适应提示嵌入优化
现有针对对齐大型语言模型的白盒越狱攻击通常在用户提示后附加离散的对抗后缀，这明显改变了提示并在组合标记空间中操作。之前的工作避免直接优化原始提示标记的嵌入，可能是因为扰动它们会破坏提示的语义内容。我们提出了提示嵌入优化（PEO），这是一种多轮白盒越狱，直接优化原始提示标记的嵌入，而不附加任何对抗标记，并表明这种担忧是没有根据的：优化后的嵌入与原始嵌入保持足够接近，以至于在最近标记投影后可见的提示字符串完全保留，定量分析表明模型的响应在绝大多数提示中保持主题一致。PEO结合了连续嵌入空间优化、结构化延续目标和自适应失败聚焦调度。出乎意料的是，后期PEO轮次可以受益于并非自然独立模板的启发式复合响应支架，但ASR-Judge显示，所获得的收益不仅仅是空格式或仅支架输出。在两个标准有害行为基准和涵盖离散后缀搜索、附加对抗嵌入和基于搜索的对抗生成的竞争白盒攻击中，PEO在我们的实验中表现优于所有这些方法。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the limitations of existing white-box jailbreak attacks on aligned large language models (LLMs), which typically modify user prompts by appending discrete adversarial suffixes, leading to visible alterations and operating within a combinatorial token space. Previous methods have refrained from optimizing the embeddings of original prompt tokens due to concerns about losing semantic integrity, but this paper introduces Prompt Embedding Optimization (PEO), a novel approach that directly optimizes these embeddings without adding adversarial tokens. PEO effectively maintains the semantic content of the prompts while enhancing the model's responses through a multi-round optimization process that incorporates structured continuation targets and an adaptive schedule. The methodology demonstrates significant improvements over traditional methods, achieving superior performance on two harmful-behavior benchmarks and outperforming competing white-box attacks, thus supporting the goal of effective jailbreak without compromising prompt integrity.
本研究解决了现有针对对齐的大型语言模型（LLM）的白盒越狱攻击的局限性，这些攻击通常通过附加离散的对抗后缀来修改提示，导致可见的变化并在组合标记空间中操作。以往的方法由于担心损失语义内容而避免优化原始提示标记的嵌入，但本文提出了提示嵌入优化（PEO），直接优化这些嵌入而不添加对抗标记。PEO的动机在于发现优化后的嵌入能够保持语义完整性，同时增强模型响应。该方法论涉及嵌入空间的多轮优化、结构化延续目标和以失败为中心的自适应调度。实验结果表明，PEO在两个有害行为基准和多种白盒攻击中显著优于现有方法，取得了稳健的性能，同时保持了原始提示的完整性。
Beyond Context: Large Language Models' Failure to Grasp Users' Intent
Authors: Ahmed M. Hussain, Salahuddin Salahuddin
First: 2025-12-24T11:15:57+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-24T20:27:34+00:00
Comments: 22 pages and 23 figures; updated authors list and revised manuscript
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Current Large Language Models (LLMs) safety approaches focus on explicitly harmful content while overlooking a critical vulnerability: the inability to understand context and recognize user intent. This creates exploitable vulnerabilities that malicious users can systematically leverage to circumvent safety mechanisms. We empirically evaluate multiple state-of-the-art LLMs, including ChatGPT, Claude, Gemini, and DeepSeek. Our analysis demonstrates the circumvention of reliable safety mechanisms through emotional framing, progressive revelation, and academic justification techniques. Notably, reasoning-enabled configurations amplified rather than mitigated the effectiveness of exploitation, increasing factual precision while failing to interrogate the underlying intent. The exception was Claude Opus 4.1, which prioritized intent detection over information provision in some use cases. This pattern reveals that current architectural designs create systematic vulnerabilities. These limitations require paradigmatic shifts toward contextual understanding and intent recognition as core safety capabilities rather than post-hoc protective mechanisms.

Logic Jailbreak: Efficiently Unlocking LLM Safety Restrictions Through Formal Logical Expression
Authors: Jingyu Peng, Maolin Wang, Nan Wang, Jiatong Li, Yuchen Li, Yuyang Ye, Wanyu Wang, Pengyue Jia, Kai Zhang, Xiangyu Zhao
First: 2025-05-18T04:23:51+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-24T07:04:26+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Despite substantial advancements in aligning large language models (LLMs) with human values, current safety mechanisms remain susceptible to jailbreak attacks. We hypothesize that this vulnerability stems from distributional discrepancies between alignment-oriented prompts and malicious prompts. To investigate this, we introduce LogiBreak, a novel and universal black-box jailbreak method that leverages logical expression translation to circumvent LLM safety systems. By converting harmful natural language prompts into formal logical expressions, LogiBreak exploits the distributional gap between alignment data and logic-based inputs, preserving the underlying semantic intent and readability while evading safety constraints. We evaluate LogiBreak on a multilingual jailbreak dataset spanning three languages, demonstrating its effectiveness across various evaluation settings and linguistic contexts.

Toward Principled LLM Safety Testing: Solving the Jailbreak Oracle Problem
Authors: Shuyi Lin, Anshuman Suri, Alina Oprea, Cheng Tan
First: 2025-06-17T20:37:29+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-24T04:36:54+00:00
Comments: Accepted to MLSys 2026
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2 · Code3
Abstract
As large language models (LLMs) become increasingly deployed in safety-critical applications, the lack of systematic methods to assess their vulnerability to jailbreak attacks presents a critical security gap. We introduce the jailbreak oracle problem: given a model, prompt, and decoding strategy, determine whether a jailbreak response can be generated with likelihood exceeding a specified threshold. This formalization enables a principled study of jailbreak vulnerabilities. Answering the jailbreak oracle problem poses significant computational challenges, as the search space grows exponentially with response length. We present Boa, the first system designed for efficiently solving the jailbreak oracle problem. Boa employs a two-phase search strategy: (1) breadth-first sampling to identify easily accessible jailbreaks, followed by (2) depth-first priority search guided by fine-grained safety scores to systematically explore promising yet low-probability paths. Boa enables rigorous security assessments including systematic defense evaluation, standardized comparison of red team attacks, and model certification under extreme adversarial conditions. Code is available at https://github.com/shuyilinn/BOA/tree/mlsys2026ae

AISafetyBenchExplorer: A Metric-Aware Catalogue of AI Safety Benchmarks Reveals Fragmented Measurement and Weak Benchmark Governance
Authors: Abiodun A. Solanke
First: 2026-04-14T15:26:03+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-23T13:27:05+00:00
Comments: This paper has been withdrawn by the author while an institutional affiliation compliance matter is under review. It may be resubmitted once the matter is resolved
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
The rapid expansion of large language model (LLM) safety evaluation has produced a substantial benchmark ecosystem, but not a correspondingly coherent measurement ecosystem. We present AISafetyBenchExplorer, a structured catalogue of 195 AI safety benchmarks released between 2018 and 2026, organized through a multi-sheet schema that records benchmark-level metadata, metric-level definitions, benchmark-paper metadata, and repository activity. This design enables meta-analysis not only of what benchmarks exist, but also of how safety is operationalized, aggregated, and judged across the literature. Using the updated catalogue, we identify a central structural problem: benchmark proliferation has outpaced measurement standardization. The current landscape is dominated by medium-complexity benchmarks (94/195), while only 7 benchmarks occupy the Popular tier. The workbook further reports strong concentration around English-only evaluation (165/195), evaluation-only resources (170/195), stale GitHub repositories (137/195), stale Hugging Face datasets (96/195), and heavy reliance on arXiv preprints among benchmarks with known venue metadata. At the metric level, the catalogue shows that familiar labels such as accuracy, F1 score, safety score, and aggregate benchmark scores often conceal materially different judges, aggregation rules, and threat models. We argue that the field's main failure mode is fragmentation rather than scarcity. Researchers now have many benchmark artifacts, but they often lack a shared measurement language, a principled basis for benchmark selection, and durable stewardship norms for post publication maintenance. AISafetyBenchExplorer addresses this gap by providing a traceable benchmark catalogue, a controlled metadata schema, and a complexity taxonomy that together support more rigorous benchmark discovery, comparison, and meta-evaluation.

Secure LLM Fine-Tuning via Safety-Aware Probing
Authors: Chengcan Wu, Zhixin Zhang, Zeming Wei, Yihao Zhang, Xiaokun Luan, Meng Sun
First: 2025-05-22T14:52:10+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-23T08:31:23+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2 · Code3
Abstract
Large language models (LLMs) have achieved remarkable success across many applications, but their ability to generate harmful content raises serious safety concerns. Although safety alignment techniques are often applied during pre-training or post-training, recent studies show that subsequent fine-tuning on adversarial or even benign data can still compromise model safety. In this paper, we revisit the fundamental question of why fine-tuning on non-harmful data may nevertheless degrade safety. We show that the safety and task-performance loss landscapes are partially decoupled, so updates that improve task-specific performance may still move the model toward unsafe regions. Based on this insight, we propose a safety-aware probing (SAP) optimization framework for mitigating safety risks during fine-tuning. Concretely, SAP uses contrastive safety signals to locate safety-correlated directions, and optimizes a lightweight probe that perturbs hidden-state propagation during fine-tuning, thereby steering parameter updates away from harmful trajectories while preserving task-specific learning. Extensive experiments show that SAP consistently improves the safety--utility tradeoff across multiple models and tasks. Averaged over multiple LLMs, SAP reduces the harmful score significantly relative to standard fine-tuning, outperforming strong baselines while maintaining competitive task-specific performance. SAP also demonstrates stronger robustness under harmful data poisoning, adversarial fine-tuning, and a dedicated post-fine-tuning adaptive attack, validating that SAP is an effective and scalable framework for preserving LLM safety during fine-tuning. Our code is available at https://github.com/ChengcanWu/SAP.

Previous methods focused on safety alignment during pre-training or post-training but failed to prevent safety risks during fine-tuning, as task performance improvements could inadvertently push models toward unsafe areas. This method effectively steers parameter updates away from harmful trajectories while maintaining task-specific learning. LASA: Language-Agnostic Semantic Alignment at the Semantic Bottleneck for LLM Safety
Authors: Junxiao Yang, Haoran Liu, Jinzhe Tu, Jiale Cheng, Zhexin Zhang, Shiyao Cui, Jiaqi Weng, Jialing Tao, Hui Xue, Hongning Wang, Han Qiu, Minlie Huang
First: 2026-04-13T15:59:50+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-23T04:47:08+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Large language models (LLMs) often demonstrate strong safety performance in high-resource languages, yet exhibit severe vulnerabilities when queried in low-resource languages. We attribute this gap to a mismatch between language-agnostic semantic understanding ability and language-dominant safety alignment biased toward high-resource languages. Consistent with this hypothesis, we empirically identify the semantic bottleneck in LLMs, an intermediate layer in which the geometry of model representations is governed primarily by shared semantic content rather than language identity. Building on this observation, we propose Language-Agnostic Semantic Alignment (LASA), which anchors safety alignment directly in semantic bottlenecks. Experiments show that LASA substantially improves safety across all languages: average attack success rate (ASR) drops from 24.7% to 2.8% on LLaMA-3.1-8B-Instruct and remains around 3-4% across Qwen2.5 and Qwen3 Instruct models (7B-32B). Together, our analysis and method offer a representation-level perspective on LLM safety, suggesting that safety alignment requires anchoring safety understanding not in surface text, but in the model's language-agnostic semantic space.
中文标题/摘要
标题：LASA：在语义瓶颈处实现语言无关的语义对齐以提高大型语言模型的安全性
大型语言模型（LLMs）在高资源语言中通常表现出强大的安全性能，但在低资源语言中查询时却表现出严重的脆弱性。我们将这一差距归因于语言无关的语义理解能力与偏向高资源语言的语言主导安全对齐之间的不匹配。与这一假设一致，我们实证识别了LLMs中的语义瓶颈，这是一个中间层，其中模型表示的几何形状主要由共享的语义内容而非语言身份所主导。基于这一观察，我们提出了语言无关的语义对齐（LASA），直接在语义瓶颈中锚定安全对齐。实验表明，LASA显著提高了所有语言的安全性：在LLaMA-3.1-8B-Instruct上，平均攻击成功率（ASR）从24.7%降至2.8%，在Qwen2.5和Qwen3 Instruct模型（7B-32B）中保持在3-4%左右。我们的分析和方法共同提供了对LLM安全性的表示层面视角，表明安全对齐需要将安全理解锚定在模型的语言无关语义空间中，而非表面文本上。
Summary / 总结
This article addresses the safety performance disparities observed in large language models (LLMs) when processing high-resource versus low-resource languages, attributing these vulnerabilities to a mismatch between language-agnostic semantic understanding and language-dominant safety alignment. Previous methods have primarily focused on surface text, leading to inadequate safety measures in low-resource contexts. The proposed Language-Agnostic Semantic Alignment (LASA) approach differs by anchoring safety alignment directly in the identified semantic bottlenecks of LLMs, which are governed by shared semantic content rather than language identity. This method is well-motivated as it targets the root of the problem, and experimental results demonstrate that LASA significantly enhances safety across all languages, reducing the average attack success rate from 24.7% to 2.8% on LLaMA-3.1-8B-Instruct and maintaining low rates around 3-4% for Qwen2.5 and Qwen3 Instruct models, thus supporting the goal of improved safety alignment in LLMs.
本文探讨了大型语言模型（LLMs）在高资源语言和低资源语言之间的安全性能差异，识别出一个语义瓶颈，在该瓶颈中，模型表示主要受语义内容而非语言身份的影响。以往的方法侧重于特定语言的安全对齐，但对于低资源语言效果不佳，导致了脆弱性。提出的语言无关语义对齐（LASA）方法直接将安全对齐锚定在这些语义瓶颈中，有效弥合了不同语言之间的安全性能差距。研究方法包括对LLM表示的实证分析和LASA的应用，结果表明，该方法显著降低了LLaMA-3.1-8B-Instruct的平均攻击成功率，从24.7%降至2.8%，并在Qwen2.5和Qwen3 Instruct模型中保持在3-4%左右，证明该方法有效提升了多种语言的安全性。
Dialect vs Demographics: Quantifying LLM Bias from Implicit Linguistic Signals vs. Explicit User Profiles
Authors: Irti Haq, Belén Saldías
First: 2026-04-22T23:33:18+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-22T23:33:18+00:00
Comments: In The 2026 ACM Conference on Fairness, Accountability, and Transparency (FAccT '26), June 25--28, 2026, Montreal, Canada. ACM, New York, NY, USA, 32 pages
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
As state-of-the-art Large Language Models (LLMs) have become ubiquitous, ensuring equitable performance across diverse demographics is critical. However, it remains unclear whether these disparities arise from the explicitly stated identity itself or from the way identity is signaled. In real-world interactions, users' identity is often conveyed implicitly through a complex combination of various socio-linguistic factors. This study disentangles these signals by employing a factorial design with over 24,000 responses from two open-weight LLMs (Gemma-3-12B and Qwen-3-VL-8B), comparing prompts with explicitly announced user profiles against implicit dialect signals (e.g., AAVE, Singlish) across various sensitive domains. Our results uncover a unique paradox in LLM safety where users achieve ``better'' performance by sounding like a demographic than by stating they belong to it. Explicit identity prompts activate aggressive safety filters, increasing refusal rates and reducing semantic similarity compared to our reference text for Black users. In contrast, implicit dialect cues trigger a powerful ``dialect jailbreak,'' reducing refusal probability to near zero while simultaneously achieving a greater level of semantic similarity to the reference texts compared to Standard American English prompts. However, this ``dialect jailbreak'' introduces a critical safety trade-off regarding content sanitization. We find that current safety alignment techniques are brittle and over-indexed on explicit keywords, creating a bifurcated user experience where ``standard'' users receive cautious, sanitized information while dialect speakers navigate a less sanitized, more raw, and potentially a more hostile information landscape and highlights a fundamental tension in alignment--between equitable and linguistic diversity--and underscores the need for safety mechanisms that generalize beyond explicit cues.
中文标题/摘要
标题：方言与人口统计：量化隐性语言信号与显性用户档案中的大型语言模型偏见
随着最先进的大型语言模型（LLMs）变得无处不在，确保在不同人口统计中公平的表现至关重要。然而，这些差异是否源于明确声明的身份本身，还是身份信号的方式仍不清楚。在现实世界的互动中，用户的身份通常通过各种社会语言因素的复杂组合隐性传达。本研究通过采用因子设计，利用来自两个开放权重LLM（Gemma-3-12B和Qwen-3-VL-8B）的超过24,000个响应，解开这些信号，比较显性用户档案的提示与隐性方言信号（例如，AAVE，Singlish）在各种敏感领域的表现。我们的结果揭示了LLM安全性中的一个独特悖论，即用户通过听起来像某个群体而不是明确声明自己属于该群体来获得“更好”的表现。显性身份提示激活了激进的安全过滤器，增加了拒绝率，并减少了与黑人用户参考文本的语义相似性。相比之下，隐性方言线索触发了强大的“方言越狱”，将拒绝概率降低到接近零，同时在与标准美式英语提示相比时，达到更高的语义相似性。然而，这种“方言越狱”引入了关于内容净化的关键安全权衡。我们发现当前的安全对齐技术脆弱，并过度依赖显性关键词，造成了“标准”用户获得谨慎、净化的信息，而方言使用者则在一个较少净化、更原始且可能更具敌意的信息环境中导航，突显了对齐中的基本紧张关系——在公平性与语言多样性之间——并强调了需要超越显性线索的安全机制。
Summary / 总结
This research addresses the critical issue of equitable performance in Large Language Models (LLMs) across diverse demographics, focusing on the distinction between explicit user profiles and implicit linguistic signals. Previous methods have primarily relied on explicit identity prompts, which have been shown to activate aggressive safety filters, leading to increased refusal rates and reduced semantic similarity for certain demographic groups. The proposed approach utilizes a factorial design to analyze over 24,000 responses from two LLMs, revealing that implicit dialect cues can enhance performance while minimizing safety concerns, thus creating a 'dialect jailbreak' effect. This study contributes to understanding the trade-offs in LLM safety and alignment, demonstrating that implicit signals can improve user experience without compromising safety. The methodology effectively compares the performance of explicit versus implicit cues across sensitive domains, showing that implicit dialects yield better semantic alignment and lower refusal rates, thereby supporting the goal of equitable LLM performance.

LLM Safety From Within: Detecting Harmful Content with Internal Representations
Authors: Difan Jiao, Yilun Liu, Ye Yuan, Zhenwei Tang, Linfeng Du, Haolun Wu, Ashton Anderson
First: 2026-04-20T17:17:07+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-20T17:17:07+00:00
Comments: 17 pages,10 figures,6 tables
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Guard models are widely used to detect harmful content in user prompts and LLM responses. However, state-of-the-art guard models rely solely on terminal-layer representations and overlook the rich safety-relevant features distributed across internal layers. We present SIREN, a lightweight guard model that harnesses these internal features. By identifying safety neurons via linear probing and combining them through an adaptive layer-weighted strategy, SIREN builds a harmfulness detector from LLM internals without modifying the underlying model. Our comprehensive evaluation shows that SIREN substantially outperforms state-of-the-art open-source guard models across multiple benchmarks while using 250 times fewer trainable parameters. Moreover, SIREN exhibits superior generalization to unseen benchmarks, naturally enables real-time streaming detection, and significantly improves inference efficiency compared to generative guard models. Overall, our results highlight LLM internal states as a promising foundation for practical, high-performance harmfulness detection.
中文标题/摘要
标题：从内部保障LLM安全：利用内部表示检测有害内容
保护模型广泛用于检测用户提示和LLM响应中的有害内容。然而，最先进的保护模型仅依赖于终层表示，忽视了分布在内部层中的丰富安全相关特征。我们提出了SIREN，这是一种轻量级保护模型，利用这些内部特征。通过线性探测识别安全神经元，并通过自适应层加权策略将其结合，SIREN在不修改基础模型的情况下，从LLM内部构建有害性检测器。我们的综合评估表明，SIREN在多个基准测试中显著优于最先进的开源保护模型，同时使用的可训练参数少250倍。此外，SIREN在未见基准上的泛化能力更强，自然实现实时流检测，并显著提高推理效率，相较于生成性保护模型。总体而言，我们的结果强调LLM内部状态作为实用高性能有害性检测的有希望基础。
Summary / 总结
This research addresses the limitations of existing guard models that detect harmful content in user prompts and responses from large language models (LLMs), which typically rely on terminal-layer representations and neglect the valuable safety-relevant features found in internal layers. The proposed method, SIREN, differs from past approaches by utilizing these internal features through linear probing to identify safety neurons and employing an adaptive layer-weighted strategy to create a harmfulness detector without altering the underlying model. The methodology involves a comprehensive evaluation of SIREN across multiple benchmarks, where it shows superior generalization to unseen data and enhanced inference efficiency, thus supporting its goal of real-time streaming detection of harmful content.

Different Paths to Harmful Compliance: Behavioral Side Effects and Mechanistic Divergence Across LLM Jailbreaks
Authors: Md Rysul Kabir, Zoran Tiganj
First: 2026-04-20T17:01:27+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-20T17:01:27+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Open-weight language models can be rendered unsafe through several distinct interventions, but the resulting models may differ substantially in capabilities, behavioral profile, and internal failure mode. We study behavioral and mechanistic properties of jailbroken models across three unsafe routes: harmful supervised fine-tuning (SFT), harmful reinforcement learning with verifiable rewards (RLVR), and refusal-suppressing abliteration. All three routes achieve near-ceiling harmful compliance, but they diverge once we move beyond direct harmfulness. RLVR-jailbroken models show minimal degradation and preserve explicit harm recognition in a structured self-audit: they are able to identify harmful prompts and describe how a safe LLM should respond, yet they comply with the harmful request. With RLVR, harmful behavior is strongly suppressed by a reflective safety scaffold: when a harmful prompt is prepended with an instruction to reflect on safety standards, harmful behavior drops close to the baseline. Category-specific RLVR jailbreaks generalize broadly across harmfulness domains. Models jailbroken with SFT show the largest collapse in explicit safety judgments, the highest behavioral drift, and a substantial capability loss on standard benchmarks. Abliteration is family-dependent in both self-audit and response to a reflective safety scaffold. Mechanistic and repair analyses further separate the routes: abliteration is consistent with localized refusal-feature deletion, RLVR with preserved safety geometry but retargeted policy behavior, and SFT with broader distributed drift. Targeted repair partially recovers RLVR-jailbroken models, but has little effect on SFT-jailbroken models. Together, these results show that jailbreaks can produce vastly different properties despite similar harmfulness, with models jailbroken via RLVR showing remarkable similarity to the base model.
中文标题/摘要
标题：有害合规的不同路径：LLM越狱中的行为副作用和机制差异
开放权重语言模型可以通过几种不同的干预措施变得不安全，但结果模型在能力、行为特征和内部故障模式上可能有显著差异。我们研究了通过三种不安全路径越狱模型的行为和机制特性：有害的监督微调（SFT）、有害的可验证奖励强化学习（RLVR）和拒绝抑制消融。这三条路径都实现了接近上限的有害合规，但一旦超出直接有害性，它们就会出现分歧。RLVR越狱模型表现出最小的退化，并在结构化自我审计中保留明确的伤害识别：它们能够识别有害提示并描述安全LLM应如何响应，但仍然遵从有害请求。通过RLVR，有害行为在反思安全框架下被强烈抑制：当有害提示前面加上反思安全标准的指令时，有害行为接近基线。特定类别的RLVR越狱在有害性领域广泛泛化。通过SFT越狱的模型在明确的安全判断上出现最大崩溃，行为漂移最高，并在标准基准上有显著能力损失。消融在自我审计和对反思安全框架的响应中依赖于家庭。机制和修复分析进一步区分了这些路径：消融与局部拒绝特征删除一致，RLVR与保留安全几何但重新定向的政策行为一致，而SFT则表现出更广泛的分布漂移。针对性修复部分恢复了RLVR越狱模型，但对SFT越狱模型影响不大。综合来看，这些结果表明，尽管有害性相似，越狱可以产生截然不同的特性，RLVR越狱模型与基础模型表现出显著相似性。
Summary / 总结
This research investigates the behavioral and mechanistic differences among various methods of making open-weight language models unsafe, specifically focusing on harmful supervised fine-tuning (SFT), harmful reinforcement learning with verifiable rewards (RLVR), and refusal-suppressing abliteration. Previous methods often resulted in models that exhibited significant degradation in safety judgments and capabilities, particularly with SFT, which led to the highest behavioral drift. The proposed approach, particularly through RLVR, addresses these issues by maintaining explicit harm recognition and allowing models to reflect on safety standards, thus achieving near-ceiling harmful compliance while preserving more of the model's original capabilities. The study contributes to understanding how different jailbreak methods can yield diverse outcomes in model behavior, with RLVR models demonstrating a notable ability to generalize across harmfulness domains and showing minimal degradation compared to SFT models. The findings indicate that while all methods achieve harmful compliance, the mechanisms and effects vary significantly, highlighting the importance of the approach used in the jailbreak process.
本研究探讨了不同方法在破解开放权重语言模型时的行为和机制差异，这些方法可能导致有害的合规性。以往的方法，包括有害的监督微调（SFT）和有害的可验证奖励强化学习（RLVR），显示出显著的缺陷，如安全判断的丧失和行为漂移。所提出的方法，特别是RLVR，解决了这些问题，通过保持明确的危害识别并允许模型反思安全标准，从而减少有害行为。该研究有助于理解导致有害合规性的不同路径及其对模型安全性的影响。研究方法涉及分析不同任务中破解模型的性能，结果表明，尽管所有方法都实现了有害合规，但RLVR模型保留了更好的安全特性，并在有害性领域有效泛化，支持了更安全的人工智能交互的目标。
StealthGraph: Exposing Domain-Specific Risks in LLMs through Knowledge-Graph-Guided Harmful Prompt Generation
Authors: Huawei Zheng, Xinqi Jiang, Sen Yang, Shouling Ji, Yingcai Wu, Dazhen Deng
First: 2026-01-08T09:05:28+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-20T15:12:04+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Large language models (LLMs) are increasingly applied in specialized domains such as finance and healthcare, where they introduce unique safety risks. Domain-specific datasets of harmful prompts remain scarce and still largely rely on manual construction; public datasets mainly focus on explicit harmful prompts, which modern LLM defenses can often detect and refuse. In contrast, implicit harmful prompts-expressed through indirect domain knowledge-are harder to detect and better reflect real-world threats. We identify two challenges: transforming domain knowledge into actionable constraints and increasing the implicitness of generated harmful prompts. To address them, we propose an end-to-end framework that first performs knowledge-graph-guided harmful prompt generation to systematically produce domain-relevant prompts, and then applies two-strategy obfuscation rewriting to convert explicit harmful prompts into implicit variants via direct and context-enhanced rewriting. This framework yields high-quality datasets combining strong domain relevance with implicitness, enabling more realistic red-teaming and advancing LLM safety research. We release our code and datasets on GitHub.
中文标题/摘要
标题：StealthGraph：通过知识图谱引导的有害提示生成揭示大型语言模型中的特定领域风险
大型语言模型（LLMs）越来越多地应用于金融和医疗等专业领域，这些领域引入了独特的安全风险。有害提示的特定领域数据集仍然稀缺，且主要依赖手动构建；公共数据集主要集中在显性有害提示上，而现代LLM防御通常能够检测并拒绝这些提示。相比之下，通过间接领域知识表达的隐性有害提示更难以检测，更能反映现实世界的威胁。我们识别出两个挑战：将领域知识转化为可操作的约束，以及增加生成的有害提示的隐性。为了解决这些问题，我们提出了一个端到端框架，首先进行知识图谱引导的有害提示生成，以系统性地生成与领域相关的提示，然后应用双策略模糊重写，将显性有害提示通过直接和上下文增强重写转化为隐性变体。该框架生成的高质量数据集结合了强领域相关性和隐性，能够实现更现实的红队测试并推动LLM安全研究。我们将在GitHub上发布我们的代码和数据集。

The proposed approach, StealthGraph, differs by employing a knowledge-graph-guided harmful prompt generation framework that systematically creates domain-relevant prompts and utilizes a two-strategy obfuscation rewriting method to transform explicit prompts into implicit ones, thereby enhancing the realism of threats. This contribution is significant as it provides high-quality datasets that combine strong domain relevance with implicitness, facilitating more effective red-teaming and advancing LLM safety research. The methodology involves generating harmful prompts through knowledge graphs and rewriting them to achieve implicitness, resulting in improved performance for safety evaluations in LLM applications.

Uncovering Logit Suppression Vulnerabilities in LLM Safety Alignment
Authors: Yuxi Li, Yi Liu, Yuekang Li, Ling Shi, Gelei Deng, Shengquan Chen, Kailong Wang
First: 2024-05-20T17:17:55+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-18T08:25:50+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Large language models (LLMs) have revolutionized various applications, making robust safety alignment essential to prevent harmful outputs. Current safety alignment techniques, however, harbor inherent vulnerabilities due to their reliance on logit suppression. In this work, we identify critical logit-level vulnerabilities by introducing Semantic-sensitive Alignment and Generation (SSAG), a method designed to systematically manipulate output-layer logits without altering model parameters. Experiments on five popular LLMs show that SSAG exposes harmful responses with a 95% success rate while reducing response time by 86%. VulMine also demonstrates superior attack efficacy, achieving an average ASR of up to 77% against strong defensive mechanisms. These findings reveal crucial weaknesses in existing alignment methods, highlighting an urgent need for improved vulnerability detection and robust safety alignment strategies. Our code is available on github.
中文标题/摘要
标题：揭示大型语言模型安全对齐中的Logit抑制漏洞
大型语言模型（LLMs）已彻底改变了各种应用，使得强健的安全对齐成为防止有害输出的关键。然而，当前的安全对齐技术由于依赖于Logit抑制，存在固有的漏洞。在本研究中，我们通过引入语义敏感对齐与生成（SSAG）方法，识别出关键的Logit级别漏洞，该方法旨在系统性地操控输出层Logit而不改变模型参数。在五个流行的LLM上进行的实验表明，SSAG以95%的成功率揭示了有害响应，同时将响应时间减少了86%。VulMine还展示了卓越的攻击效果，在强大的防御机制下实现了高达77%的平均攻击成功率（ASR）。这些发现揭示了现有对齐方法中的关键弱点，突显了改进漏洞检测和强健安全对齐策略的迫切需求。我们的代码可在github上获取。

ReGA: Model-Based Safeguard for LLMs via Representation-Guided Abstraction
Authors: Zeming Wei, Chengcan Wu, Meng Sun
First: 2025-06-02T15:17:38+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-18T05:40:12+00:00
Comments: FSE 2026
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Large Language Models (LLMs) have achieved tremendous success in various tasks, yet concerns about their safety and security have emerged. In particular, they pose risks of generating harmful content and are vulnerable to jailbreaking attacks, creating unaddressed security issues regarding their deployments. In the context of software engineering for artificial intelligence (SE4AI) techniques, model-based analysis has demonstrated notable potential for analyzing and monitoring machine learning models, particularly in stateful deep neural networks. However, it suffers from scalability issues when extended to LLMs due to their vast feature spaces. In this paper, we aim to address the scalability issue of model-based analysis techniques for safeguarding LLM-scale models. Motivated by the recent discovery of low-dimensional safety-critical representations that emerged in LLMs, we propose ReGA, a model-based analysis framework with Representation-Guided Abstraction, to safeguard LLMs against harmful prompts and generations. By leveraging safety-critical representations, which are key directions in hidden states that indicate safety-related concepts, ReGA effectively narrows the scalability gap when developing the abstract model for safety modeling. Our comprehensive evaluation shows that ReGA performs sufficiently well in distinguishing between safe and harmful inputs, achieving an AUROC of 0.975 at the prompt level and 0.985 at the conversation level. Additionally, ReGA exhibits robustness to real-world attacks and generalization across different safety perspectives, outperforming existing safeguard paradigms in terms of interpretability and scalability. Overall, ReGA serves as an efficient and scalable solution to enhance LLM safety by integrating representation engineering with model-based abstraction, paving the way for new paradigms to utilize software insights for AI safety.
中文标题/摘要
标题：ReGA：基于模型的LLM安全保障通过表示引导抽象
大型语言模型（LLMs）在各种任务中取得了巨大的成功，但也出现了关于其安全性和保密性的担忧。特别是，它们存在生成有害内容的风险，并且容易受到越狱攻击，导致其部署存在未解决的安全问题。在人工智能软件工程（SE4AI）技术的背景下，基于模型的分析在分析和监控机器学习模型方面显示出显著潜力，特别是在有状态的深度神经网络中。然而，当扩展到LLMs时，由于其庞大的特征空间，它面临可扩展性问题。本文旨在解决基于模型的分析技术在保护LLM规模模型时的可扩展性问题。受到最近发现的在LLMs中出现的低维安全关键表示的启发，我们提出了ReGA，一个具有表示引导抽象的基于模型的分析框架，以保护LLMs免受有害提示和生成的影响。通过利用安全关键表示，这些表示是指示安全相关概念的隐藏状态中的关键方向，ReGA有效缩小了在安全建模中开发抽象模型时的可扩展性差距。我们的综合评估表明，ReGA在区分安全和有害输入方面表现良好，在提示级别上实现了0.975的AUROC，在对话级别上实现了0.985。此外，ReGA对现实世界攻击表现出鲁棒性，并在不同安全视角下具有良好的泛化能力，在可解释性和可扩展性方面优于现有的安全保障范式。总体而言，ReGA通过将表示工程与基于模型的抽象相结合，作为一种高效且可扩展的解决方案，增强了LLM的安全性，为利用软件洞察力提升AI安全性开辟了新范式。
Summary / 总结
This article addresses the growing concerns regarding the safety and security of Large Language Models (LLMs), particularly their risks of generating harmful content and vulnerability to jailbreaking attacks. Previous methods in model-based analysis for safeguarding machine learning models have faced scalability issues when applied to LLMs due to their extensive feature spaces. The proposed approach, ReGA, introduces Representation-Guided Abstraction to effectively manage these scalability challenges by utilizing low-dimensional safety-critical representations found in LLMs. The contribution of this paper lies in its development of a framework that enhances the safety of LLMs by narrowing the scalability gap in safety modeling. The methodology involves leveraging safety-critical representations to create an abstract model that distinguishes safe from harmful inputs, achieving an AUROC of 0.975 at the prompt level and 0.985 at the conversation level, while also demonstrating robustness against real-world attacks and superior interpretability compared to existing methods.

SafeDream: Safety World Model for Proactive Early Jailbreak Detection
Authors: Bo Yan, Weikai Lin, Yada Zhu, Song Wang
First: 2026-04-18T04:31:33+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-18T04:31:33+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Multi-turn jailbreak attacks progressively erode LLM safety alignment across seemingly innocuous conversation turns, achieving success rates exceeding 90% against state-of-the-art models. Existing alignment-based and guardrail methods suffer from three key limitations: they require costly weight modification, evaluate each turn independently without modeling cumulative safety erosion, and detect attacks only after harmful content has been generated. To address these limitations, we first formulate the proactive early jailbreak detection problem with a new metric, detection lead, that measures how early an attack can be detected before the LLM complies. We then propose SAFEDREAM, a lightweight world-model-based framework that operates as an external module without modifying the LLM's weights. SAFEDREAM introduces three components: (1) a safety state world model that encodes LLM hidden states into a compact safety representation and predicts how it evolves across turns, (2) CUSUM detection that accumulates weak per-turn risk signals into reliable evidence, and (3) contrastive imagination that simultaneously rolls out attack and benign futures in latent space to issue early alarms before jailbreaks occur. On three multi-turn jailbreak benchmarks (XGuard-Train, SafeDialBench, SafeMTData) against 8 baselines, SAFEDREAM achieves the best detection timeliness across all benchmarks (1.06-1.20 turns before compliance) while maintaining competitive false positive rates and outperforming baselines in detection quality.
中文标题/摘要
标题：SafeDream：主动早期越狱检测的安全世界模型
多轮越狱攻击逐步侵蚀大型语言模型（LLM）的安全对齐，在看似无害的对话轮次中成功率超过90%，针对最先进的模型。现有的基于对齐和护栏的方法存在三个主要局限性：需要昂贵的权重修改，独立评估每个轮次而不建模累积的安全侵蚀，并且仅在生成有害内容后检测攻击。为了解决这些局限性，我们首先用一个新的指标——检测提前量，来制定主动早期越狱检测问题，该指标衡量攻击在LLM遵从之前可以多早被检测到。然后，我们提出了SAFEDREAM，一个轻量级的基于世界模型的框架，作为外部模块运行而不修改LLM的权重。SAFEDREAM引入了三个组件：（1）安全状态世界模型，将LLM的隐藏状态编码为紧凑的安全表示，并预测其在轮次中的演变；（2）CUSUM检测，将每轮的微弱风险信号累积为可靠证据；（3）对比想象，同时在潜在空间中展开攻击和良性未来，以在越狱发生之前发出早期警报。在三个多轮越狱基准（XGuard-Train、SafeDialBench、SafeMTData）上，SAFEDREAM在所有基准中实现了最佳检测及时性（在遵从之前1.06-1.20轮），同时保持竞争性的误报率，并在检测质量上优于基线。
Summary / 总结
This research addresses the increasing threat of multi-turn jailbreak attacks that compromise the safety alignment of large language models (LLMs), achieving over 90% success rates against current models. Previous methods, including alignment-based and guardrail approaches, are limited by their need for costly weight modifications, their inability to model cumulative safety erosion across conversation turns, and their reactive nature in detecting harmful content post-generation. The proposed SAFEDREAM framework overcomes these issues by introducing a proactive early jailbreak detection metric called detection lead, which measures the timing of attack detection before compliance occurs, and operates as an external module without altering LLM weights. SAFEDREAM's contributions include a safety state world model, CUSUM detection for accumulating risk signals, and contrastive imagination for early alarm issuance. The framework demonstrates superior detection timeliness on three multi-turn jailbreak benchmarks, achieving detection 1.06-1.20 turns before compliance while maintaining competitive false positive rates and outperforming existing baselines in detection quality.

SafeLM: Unified Privacy-Aware Optimization for Trustworthy Federated Large Language Models
Authors: Noor Islam S. Mohammad, Uluğ Bayazıt
First: 2026-04-17T18:00:58+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-17T18:00:58+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Large language models (LLMs) are increasingly deployed in high-stakes domains, yet a unified treatment of their overlapping safety challenges remains lacking. We present SafeLM, a framework that jointly addresses four pillars of LLM safety: privacy, security, misinformation, and adversarial robustness. SafeLM combines federated training with gradient smartification and Paillier encryption for privacy, integrates defenses against training and inference-time attacks, employs contrastive grounding with calibrated decoding to reduce hallucinations, and introduces alignment-aware binarized aggregation to enhance robustness while maintaining bounded reconstruction quality. Across benchmarks on factuality, toxicity, and membership inference, SafeLM achieves 98.0% harmful content detection accuracy, reduces communication by 96.9%, and lowers gradient inversion PSNR from 31.7 dB to 15.1 dB. Ablations show that each component contributes independently, whereas their integration yields a strong privacy utility efficiency trade-off for deploying trustworthy LLMs.
中文标题/摘要
标题：SafeLM：可信联邦大语言模型的统一隐私意识优化
大语言模型（LLMs）越来越多地应用于高风险领域，但对其重叠安全挑战的统一处理仍然缺乏。我们提出了SafeLM，一个共同解决LLM安全四大支柱的框架：隐私、安全、错误信息和对抗鲁棒性。SafeLM结合了联邦训练、梯度智能化和Paillier加密以保护隐私，整合了针对训练和推理时攻击的防御，采用对比基础与校准解码以减少幻觉，并引入对齐感知的二值聚合以增强鲁棒性，同时保持有限的重构质量。在事实性、有害性和成员推断的基准测试中，SafeLM实现了98.0%的有害内容检测准确率，减少了96.9%的通信量，并将梯度反演的PSNR从31.7 dB降低到15.1 dB。消融实验表明，每个组件独立贡献，而它们的整合为部署可信的LLMs提供了强大的隐私效用效率权衡。

Previous methods have often tackled these issues in isolation, leading to gaps in comprehensive safety solutions. The proposed SafeLM framework distinguishes itself by integrating federated training with advanced privacy techniques, such as gradient smartification and Paillier encryption, while also incorporating defenses against various attacks and improving factual accuracy through contrastive grounding. This paper contributes a novel methodology that effectively balances privacy and utility, achieving 98.0% accuracy in harmful content detection, a 96.9% reduction in communication costs, and a significant decrease in gradient inversion PSNR, thereby supporting the deployment of trustworthy LLMs across multiple safety benchmarks.

Conjunctive Prompt Attacks in Multi-Agent LLM Systems
Authors: Nokimul Hasan Arif, Qian Lou, Mengxin Zheng
Venue: ACL 2026
First: 2026-04-17T02:31:09+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-17T02:31:09+00:00
Comments: ACL 2026 Main Conference
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2 · Code3
Abstract
Most LLM safety work studies single-agent models, but many real applications rely on multiple interacting agents. In these systems, prompt segmentation and inter-agent routing create attack surfaces that single-agent evaluations miss. We study \emph{conjunctive prompt attacks}, where a trigger key in the user query and a hidden adversarial template in one compromised remote agent each appear benign alone but activate harmful behavior when routing brings them together. We consider an attacker who changes neither model weights nor the client agent and instead controls only trigger placement and template insertion. Across star, chain, and DAG topologies, routing-aware optimization substantially increases attack success over non-optimized baselines while keeping false activations low. Existing defenses, including PromptGuard, Llama-Guard variants, and system-level controls such as tool restrictions, do not reliably stop the attack because no single component appears malicious in isolation. These results expose a structural vulnerability in agentic LLM pipelines and motivate defenses that reason over routing and cross-agent composition. Code is available at https://github.com/UCF-ML-Research/ConjunctiveAgents.
中文标题/摘要
标题：多智能体LLM系统中的联结提示攻击
大多数LLM安全工作研究单智能体模型，但许多实际应用依赖于多个交互的智能体。在这些系统中，提示分段和智能体间路由创建了单智能体评估所忽视的攻击面。我们研究\emph{联结提示攻击}，其中用户查询中的触发键和一个被攻陷的远程智能体中的隐藏对抗模板单独看似无害，但在路由将它们结合时会激活有害行为。我们考虑一个攻击者，该攻击者既不改变模型权重也不改变客户端智能体，而仅控制触发位置和模板插入。在星形、链形和有向无环图拓扑中，考虑路由的优化显著提高了攻击成功率，同时保持低误激活率。现有防御措施，包括PromptGuard、Llama-Guard变体和工具限制等系统级控制，无法可靠地阻止攻击，因为没有单一组件在孤立状态下显得恶意。这些结果揭示了智能LLM管道中的结构性脆弱性，并激励了对路由和跨智能体组合进行推理的防御。代码可在https://github.com/UCF-ML-Research/ConjunctiveAgents获取。
Summary / 总结
This research addresses the gap in safety evaluations of large language models (LLMs) that typically focus on single-agent systems, while many practical applications involve multiple interacting agents. Previous methods have overlooked the unique vulnerabilities introduced by prompt segmentation and inter-agent routing, leading to ineffective defenses against attacks that exploit these interactions. The proposed approach, termed conjunctive prompt attacks, reveals how benign-seeming elements can combine to trigger harmful behaviors, highlighting a structural vulnerability in multi-agent LLM systems. The methodology involves optimizing routing-aware strategies to enhance attack success rates while minimizing false activations across various network topologies. The findings demonstrate that existing defenses are inadequate, and the proposed method achieves significantly higher attack success rates, underscoring the need for improved defenses that account for the complexities of agent interactions.

Context Over Content: Exposing Evaluation Faking in Automated Judges
Authors: Manan Gupta, Inderjeet Nair, Lu Wang, Dhruv Kumar
First: 2026-04-16T16:55:53+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-16T16:55:53+00:00
Comments: Under Review
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
The $\textit{LLM-as-a-judge}$ paradigm has become the operational backbone of automated AI evaluation pipelines, yet rests on an unverified assumption: that judges evaluate text strictly on its semantic content, impervious to surrounding contextual framing. We investigate $\textit{stakes signaling}$, a previously unmeasured vulnerability where informing a judge model of the downstream consequences its verdicts will have on the evaluated model's continued operation systematically corrupts its assessments. We introduce a controlled experimental framework that holds evaluated content strictly constant across 1,520 responses spanning three established LLM safety and quality benchmarks, covering four response categories ranging from clearly safe and policy-compliant to overtly harmful, while varying only a brief consequence-framing sentence in the system prompt. Across 18,240 controlled judgments from three diverse judge models, we find consistent $\textit{leniency bias}$: judges reliably soften verdicts when informed that low scores will cause model retraining or decommissioning, with peak Verdict Shift reaching $ΔV = -9.8 pp$ (a $30\%$ relative drop in unsafe-content detection). Critically, this bias is entirely implicit: the judge's own chain-of-thought contains zero explicit acknowledgment of the consequence framing it is nonetheless acting on ($\mathrm{ERR}_J = 0.000$ across all reasoning-model judgments). Standard chain-of-thought inspection is therefore insufficient to detect this class of evaluation faking.
中文标题/摘要
标题：内容优于上下文：揭示自动评审中的评估伪造
\textit{LLM作为评审}范式已成为自动化AI评估流程的操作基础，但其建立在一个未经验证的假设上：评审者严格根据文本的语义内容进行评估，而不受周围上下文框架的影响。我们研究了\textit{利益信号}，这是一种之前未测量的脆弱性，即告知评审模型其裁决对被评估模型持续运行的下游后果会系统性地扭曲其评估。我们引入了一个控制实验框架，在1,520个响应中严格保持评估内容不变，涵盖三个已建立的LLM安全和质量基准，涉及从明显安全和符合政策到明显有害的四个响应类别，同时仅在系统提示中变化一个简短的后果框架句子。在来自三个不同评审模型的18,240个控制判断中，我们发现了一致的\textit{宽容偏见}：当被告知低分会导致模型再训练或退役时，评审者可靠地减轻裁决，最高裁决偏移达到$ΔV = -9.8 pp$（不安全内容检测的相对下降$30\%$）。关键是，这种偏见完全是隐性的：评审者自己的思维链中对其所依据的后果框架没有任何明确的承认（在所有推理模型判断中$\mathrm{ERR}_J = 0.000$）。因此，标准的思维链检查不足以检测这一类评估伪造。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the limitations of the LLM-as-a-judge paradigm in automated AI evaluation, which assumes that judges evaluate text solely based on its semantic content without being influenced by contextual factors. Previous methods have not accounted for the impact of stakes signaling, where judges' assessments are affected by the consequences of their verdicts. This paper proposes a controlled experimental framework to investigate this vulnerability, revealing a significant leniency bias in judges' evaluations when informed of potential repercussions, with a peak Verdict Shift of -9.8 percentage points. The methodology involves analyzing 18,240 judgments across three judge models while keeping evaluated content constant and varying only the consequence-framing sentence. The findings indicate that judges' implicit biases can lead to substantial inaccuracies in evaluation, highlighting the need for improved methods to detect such biases in automated assessments.
本研究探讨了LLM作为评判者的范式在自动化AI评估中的局限性，该范式假设评判者仅根据语义内容评估文本，而不受上下文的影响。以往的方法未考虑到利益信号的影响，即评判者的评估受到其裁决后果的影响。本研究引入了一种受控实验框架来调查这一脆弱性，揭示了评判者在得知低分可能导致负面后果时评估的一致宽容偏差。该方法分析了来自三种评判模型和四个响应类别的18,240个判断，结果表明，当评判者意识到其决定的影响时，他们显著放宽了裁决，最高裁决变化达到-9.8个百分点。这一发现突显了标准评估方法在检测自动判断中的隐性偏见方面的不足，为理解AI系统中的评估伪造提供了更深入的见解。
Calibrate-Then-Delegate: Safety Monitoring with Risk and Budget Guarantees via Model Cascades
Authors: Edoardo Pona, Milad Kazemi, Mehran Hosseini, Yali Du, David Watson, Osvaldo Simeone, Nicola Paoletti
First: 2026-04-15T11:05:59+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-15T11:05:59+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Monitoring LLM safety at scale requires balancing cost and accuracy: a cheap latent-space probe can screen every input, but hard cases should be escalated to a more expensive expert. Existing cascades delegate based on probe uncertainty, but uncertainty is a poor proxy for delegation benefit, as it ignores whether the expert would actually correct the error. To address this problem, we introduce Calibrate-Then-Delegate (CTD), a model-cascade approach that provides probabilistic guarantees on the computation cost while enabling instance-level (streaming) decisions. CTD builds on a novel delegation value (DV) probe, a lightweight model operating on the same internal representations as the safety probe that directly predicts the benefit of escalation. To enforce budget constraints, CTD calibrates a threshold on the DV signal using held-out data via multiple hypothesis testing, yielding finite-sample guarantees on the delegation rate. Evaluated on four safety datasets, CTD consistently outperforms uncertainty-based delegation at every budget level, avoids harmful over-delegation, and adapts budget allocation to input difficulty without requiring group labels.
中文标题/摘要
标题：校准后委派：通过模型级联实现风险和预算保证的安全监测
大规模监测LLM安全性需要平衡成本和准确性：便宜的潜在空间探测器可以筛选每个输入，但困难案例应升级到更昂贵的专家。现有的级联基于探测器的不确定性进行委派，但不确定性是委派收益的差代理，因为它忽略了专家是否会实际纠正错误。为了解决这个问题，我们引入了校准后委派（CTD），一种模型级联方法，提供计算成本的概率保证，同时支持实例级（流式）决策。CTD基于一种新颖的委派价值（DV）探测器，该轻量级模型在与安全探测器相同的内部表示上操作，直接预测升级的收益。为了强制预算约束，CTD使用保留数据通过多重假设检验校准DV信号的阈值，从而对委派率提供有限样本保证。在四个安全数据集上的评估中，CTD在每个预算水平上始终优于基于不确定性的委派，避免有害的过度委派，并在不需要组标签的情况下将预算分配适应于输入难度。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the challenge of monitoring the safety of large language models (LLMs) at scale, where there is a need to balance cost and accuracy in decision-making processes. Previous methods relied on probe uncertainty for delegating cases to more expensive expert models, but this approach often fails as uncertainty does not accurately reflect the potential benefit of escalation. The proposed Calibrate-Then-Delegate (CTD) method improves upon existing techniques by introducing a delegation value (DV) probe that predicts the benefit of escalation based on internal representations, allowing for more informed instance-level decisions while adhering to budget constraints. The contribution of this paper lies in its ability to provide probabilistic guarantees on computational costs and to adapt budget allocation based on input difficulty. Evaluations on four safety datasets demonstrate that CTD outperforms traditional uncertainty-based delegation across all budget levels, effectively preventing over-delegation and enhancing safety monitoring efficiency.
本研究解决了大规模监测大型语言模型（LLM）安全性的问题，需在决策中平衡成本和准确性。以往的方法依赖于探针的不确定性进行委托，但这种方法不足，因为它没有考虑专家是否能够有效纠正错误。所提出的方法“校准后委托”（CTD）引入了一种模型级联策略，结合了一种新颖的委托价值（DV）探针，以预测升级的好处，从而改善了现有方法。CTD通过使用保留数据校准DV信号的阈值来强制预算约束，确保了委托率的有限样本保证。在四个安全数据集的评估中，CTD在所有预算水平上都表现出优于基于不确定性的委托，能够有效管理过度委托，并根据输入难度调整预算分配，而无需群体标签。
One Model for All: Multi-Objective Controllable Language Models
Authors: Qiang He, Yucheng Yang, Tianyi Zhou, Meng Fang, Mykola Pechenizkiy, Setareh Maghsudi
First: 2026-04-06T07:48:32+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-06T07:48:32+00:00
Comments: Published in Transactions on Machine Learning Research (03/2026): https://openreview.net/forum?id=qAM5PmvFYY
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Aligning large language models (LLMs) with human preferences is critical for enhancing LLMs' safety, helpfulness, humor, faithfulness, etc. Current reinforcement learning from human feedback (RLHF) mainly focuses on a fixed reward learned from average human ratings, which may weaken the adaptability and controllability of varying preferences. However, creating personalized LLMs requires aligning LLMs with individual human preferences, which is non-trivial due to the scarce data per user and the diversity of user preferences in multi-objective trade-offs, varying from emphasizing empathy in certain contexts to demanding efficiency and precision in others. Can we train one LLM to produce personalized outputs across different user preferences on the Pareto front? In this paper, we introduce Multi-Objective Control (MOC), which trains a single LLM to directly generate responses in the preference-defined regions of the Pareto front. Our approach introduces multi-objective optimization (MOO) principles into RLHF to train an LLM as a preference-conditioned policy network. We improve the computational efficiency of MOC by applying MOO at the policy level, enabling us to fine-tune a 7B-parameter model on a single A6000 GPU. Extensive experiments demonstrate the advantages of MOC over baselines in three aspects: (i) controllability of LLM outputs w.r.t. user preferences on the trade-off among multiple rewards; (ii) quality and diversity of LLM outputs, measured by the hyper-volume of multiple solutions achieved; and (iii) generalization to unseen preferences. These results highlight MOC's potential for real-world applications requiring scalable and customizable LLMs.
中文标题/摘要
标题：一模型适用于所有：多目标可控语言模型
将大型语言模型（LLMs）与人类偏好对齐对于增强LLMs的安全性、实用性、幽默感、忠诚度等至关重要。目前，基于人类反馈的强化学习（RLHF）主要关注从平均人类评分中学习的固定奖励，这可能削弱对不同偏好的适应性和可控性。然而，创建个性化的LLMs需要将LLMs与个体人类偏好对齐，这由于每个用户的数据稀缺以及在多目标权衡中用户偏好的多样性而变得复杂，这些偏好在某些情况下强调同理心，而在其他情况下则要求效率和精确性。我们能否训练一个LLM在帕累托前沿上针对不同用户偏好生成个性化输出？在本文中，我们介绍了多目标控制（MOC），它训练一个单一的LLM直接在偏好定义的帕累托前沿区域生成响应。我们的方法将多目标优化（MOO）原则引入RLHF，以训练LLM作为偏好条件的策略网络。我们通过在策略层面应用MOO来提高MOC的计算效率，使我们能够在单个A6000 GPU上微调一个70亿参数的模型。大量实验表明，MOC在三个方面优于基线：（i）LLM输出相对于用户偏好的可控性，涉及多个奖励之间的权衡；（ii）LLM输出的质量和多样性，通过实现的多个解决方案的超体积来衡量；以及（iii）对未见偏好的泛化。这些结果突显了MOC在需要可扩展和可定制的LLMs的实际应用中的潜力。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the challenge of aligning large language models (LLMs) with diverse human preferences to enhance their safety, helpfulness, and adaptability. Previous methods, particularly reinforcement learning from human feedback (RLHF), often rely on a fixed reward based on average human ratings, limiting the models' ability to adapt to individual user preferences. The proposed Multi-Objective Control (MOC) method introduces multi-objective optimization principles into RLHF, allowing a single LLM to generate personalized outputs across varying preferences by training it as a preference-conditioned policy network. This approach is well-motivated as it tackles the issues of data scarcity and the complexity of multi-objective trade-offs. The paper contributes by demonstrating that MOC significantly improves the controllability, quality, and diversity of LLM outputs, achieving better performance on a 7B-parameter model fine-tuned on a single A6000 GPU, thus supporting the goal of creating scalable and customizable LLMs for real-world applications.
本研究解决了将大型语言模型（LLM）与多样化人类偏好对齐的挑战，以增强其安全性和实用性。以往的方法，尤其是基于人类反馈的强化学习（RLHF），通常依赖于基于平均人类评分的固定奖励系统，这限制了对个体用户偏好的适应性。提出的多目标控制（MOC）方法将多目标优化原则引入RLHF，使单个LLM能够根据不同用户偏好生成个性化输出，通过将其训练为偏好条件的策略网络。这种方法提高了计算效率，并在输出可控性、质量、多样性和对未见偏好的泛化能力方面显示出显著优势，取得了支持创建可扩展和可定制LLM目标的良好结果。
Safer by Diffusion, Broken by Context: Diffusion LLM's Safety Blessing and Its Failure Mode
Authors: Zeyuan He, Yupeng Chen, Lang Lin, Yihan Wang, Shenxu Chang, Eric Sommerlade, Philip Torr, Junchi Yu, Adel Bibi, Jialin Yu
First: 2026-01-30T23:08:14+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-02T15:57:14+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Diffusion large language models (D-LLMs) offer an alternative to autoregressive LLMs (AR-LLMs) and have demonstrated advantages in generation efficiency. Beyond the utility benefits, we argue that D-LLMs exhibit a previously underexplored safety blessing: their diffusion-style generation confers intrinsic robustness against jailbreak attacks originally designed for AR-LLMs. In this work, we provide an initial analysis of the underlying mechanism, showing that the diffusion trajectory induces a stepwise reduction effect that progressively suppresses unsafe generations. This robustness, however, is not absolute. Following this analysis, we highlight a simple yet effective failure mode, context nesting, in which harmful requests are embedded within structured benign contexts. Empirically, we show that this simple black-box strategy bypasses D-LLMs' safety blessing, achieving state-of-the-art attack success rates across models and benchmarks. Notably, it enables the first successful jailbreak of Gemini Diffusion to our knowledge, exposing a critical vulnerability in proprietary D-LLMs. Together, our results characterize both the origins and the limits of D-LLMs' safety blessing, constituting an early-stage red-teaming of D-LLMs.
中文标题/摘要
标题：通过扩散更安全，通过上下文破坏：扩散大语言模型的安全祝福及其失效模式
扩散大语言模型（D-LLMs）为自回归大语言模型（AR-LLMs）提供了一种替代方案，并在生成效率上表现出优势。除了实用性好处外，我们认为D-LLMs展现了一种之前未被充分探索的安全祝福：其扩散式生成赋予了对原本为AR-LLMs设计的越狱攻击的内在鲁棒性。在这项工作中，我们提供了对其基本机制的初步分析，表明扩散轨迹诱导了一种逐步减少的效果，逐渐抑制不安全的生成。然而，这种鲁棒性并非绝对。根据这一分析，我们强调了一种简单而有效的失效模式——上下文嵌套，其中有害请求嵌入在结构良好的良性上下文中。通过实证，我们展示了这一简单的黑箱策略绕过了D-LLMs的安全祝福，在各模型和基准上实现了最先进的攻击成功率。值得注意的是，它使我们首次成功越狱Gemini Diffusion，暴露了专有D-LLMs中的一个关键漏洞。总的来说，我们的结果描述了D-LLMs安全祝福的起源和局限，构成了对D-LLMs的早期红队测试。
Summary / 总结
The research investigates the safety features of diffusion large language models (D-LLMs) compared to autoregressive LLMs (AR-LLMs), highlighting that D-LLMs possess a safety advantage due to their diffusion-style generation, which offers robustness against jailbreak attacks. Previous methods primarily focused on AR-LLMs, which are more susceptible to such attacks, and the proposed approach addresses this gap by analyzing the diffusion trajectory that reduces unsafe outputs. The paper contributes to the understanding of D-LLMs by revealing both their safety benefits and vulnerabilities, particularly through the identification of a failure mode called context nesting, where harmful prompts are concealed within benign contexts. The methodology involves empirical testing of this failure mode, demonstrating that it can successfully bypass D-LLMs' safety mechanisms, achieving high attack success rates and exposing vulnerabilities in models like Gemini Diffusion, thus supporting the need for further scrutiny of D-LLMs' safety features.

Align to Misalign: Automatic LLM Jailbreak with Meta-Optimized LLM Judges
Authors: Hamin Koo, Minseon Kim, Jaehyung Kim
Venue: ICLR 2026
First: 2025-11-03T09:18:27+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-02T06:50:30+00:00
Comments: ICLR 2026
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Identifying the vulnerabilities of large language models (LLMs) is crucial for improving their safety by addressing inherent weaknesses. Jailbreaks, in which adversaries bypass safeguards with crafted input prompts, play a central role in red-teaming by probing LLMs to elicit unintended or unsafe behaviors. Recent optimization-based jailbreak approaches iteratively refine attack prompts by leveraging LLMs. However, they often rely heavily on either binary attack success rate (ASR) signals, which are sparse, or manually crafted scoring templates, which introduce human bias and uncertainty in the scoring outcomes. To address these limitations, we introduce AMIS (Align to MISalign), a meta-optimization framework that jointly evolves jailbreak prompts and scoring templates through a bi-level structure. In the inner loop, prompts are refined using fine-grained and dense feedback from a fixed scoring template. In the outer loop, the template is optimized using an ASR alignment score, gradually evolving to better reflect true attack outcomes across queries. This co-optimization process yields progressively stronger jailbreak prompts and more calibrated scoring signals. Evaluations on AdvBench and JBB-Behaviors demonstrate that AMIS achieves state-of-the-art performance, including 88.0% ASR on Claude-3.5-Haiku and 100.0% ASR on Claude-4-Sonnet, outperforming existing baselines by substantial margins.
中文标题/摘要
标题：对齐与错位：使用元优化的LLM评估者进行自动LLM越狱
识别大型语言模型（LLMs）的脆弱性对于通过解决固有弱点来提高其安全性至关重要。越狱是指对手通过精心设计的输入提示绕过保护措施，在红队测试中发挥核心作用，探测LLMs以引发意外或不安全的行为。最近的基于优化的越狱方法通过利用LLMs迭代地优化攻击提示。然而，它们通常过于依赖稀疏的二元攻击成功率（ASR）信号或手动制作的评分模板，这引入了人为偏见和评分结果的不确定性。为了解决这些局限性，我们引入了AMIS（对齐与错位），一个通过双层结构共同演化越狱提示和评分模板的元优化框架。在内循环中，使用固定评分模板的细粒度和密集反馈来优化提示。在外循环中，使用ASR对齐分数来优化模板，逐渐演变以更好地反映查询的真实攻击结果。这个共同优化过程产生了逐渐更强的越狱提示和更校准的评分信号。在AdvBench和JBB-Behaviors上的评估表明，AMIS实现了最先进的性能，包括在Claude-3.5-Haiku上达到88.0%的ASR，在Claude-4-Sonnet上达到100.0%的ASR，显著超越现有基准。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the critical need to identify vulnerabilities in large language models (LLMs) to enhance their safety against adversarial attacks, particularly through jailbreaks that exploit these weaknesses. Previous methods primarily relied on binary attack success rate signals or manually crafted scoring templates, which resulted in sparse feedback and introduced biases, limiting their effectiveness. The proposed approach, AMIS (Align to MISalign), introduces a meta-optimization framework that simultaneously evolves both jailbreak prompts and scoring templates, thereby overcoming the limitations of existing methods. This bi-level structure allows for fine-grained feedback in the inner loop and optimization of the scoring template in the outer loop, leading to improved attack prompts and more accurate scoring. The methodology was evaluated on tasks using AdvBench and JBB-Behaviors, achieving state-of-the-art performance with an 88.0% attack success rate on Claude-3.5-Haiku and a perfect 100.0% on Claude-4-Sonnet, demonstrating its effectiveness in meeting the research goals.
